			<div class="comment-content"><p>And speaking of bigger things, the size of the monsters poses an interesting question for the Godzilla threshold in Twig.  The first monster is already twice the size of a large horse (which is quite big &#8211; <a href="http://i222.photobucket.com/albums/dd199/kamaloo/diggerthehorse_01.jpg" rel="nofollow">http://i222.photobucket.com/albums/dd199/kamaloo/diggerthehorse_01.jpg</a>).  This thing is a mix of green anaconda and something from the cat family &#8211; presumably a large python.  </p>
<p>Other comments: genetics are real or at least a discipline in-universe and latin names corresponding to &#8220;our world&#8221; are utilized.  Open questions of where you get the materials to make these experiments.  I&#8217;d wager the Academy is covertly supplying people in order to drive testing and experimentation.  Not clear why they want to pay to shut it down.  Vg unf rpubrf gb Rqra naq Mvba ehaavat grfgf ba uhznavgl guebhtu pbasyvpg.</p>
<p>The kids have also been working together for years (that seems to imply 3-4) so potentially they banded together at 7/8/9 years old and have survived and thrived this long.</p>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>The about page shows &#8220;mutterings of work taken by ‘stitched’ men of patchwork flesh that do not need to sleep&#8221; which has parallels to fears of automation and factories happening at this time.  It indicates mechanization and industrialization is performed by the stitched creations.  </p>
<p>Also &#8211; Wildbow pretty actively stays away from sexual topics, again as indicated by the about page.  The repeated reference to looking up skirts might have some reference to how they are all stitched together or are not completely natural &#8211; e.g. it might not be at all sexual (particularly given age of the children).  Furthermore, it&#8217;s a bit weird that both of the girls are wearing skirts, when they are out climbing around and fighting a monster.  I understand gender norms were stronger back then, but for a group of swashbuckling orphans to enforce them is a little strange.</p>
</div>

		<article id="comment-188" class="comment">
			<footer>
				<div class="comment-author vcard">
					<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/30c18c4fe0b8425ff0d3055fb9909b9b?s=50&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-50' height='50' width='50' />					<cite class="fn"><a href='http://bakerjake.wordpress.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>bakerjake</a></cite> |
					<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
						<a href="https://twigserial.wordpress.com/2014/12/24/taking-root-1-1/#comment-188"><time pubdate datetime="2015-03-10T15:06:39+00:00">
						March 10, 2015 at 3:06 pm						</time></a>
											</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->

				</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard -->
							</footer>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>The connection of Sy to Twig is embodied in the name Sylvester: <a href="http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=Sylvester" rel="nofollow">http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=Sylvester</a></p>
<p>masc. proper name, from Latin silvestris, literally &#8220;of a wood, of a forest, woody, rural, pastoral,&#8221; from silva &#8220;wood, forest&#8221; (see sylvan). St. Sylvester&#8217;s Day is Dec. 31.</p>
<p>This would seem to indicate more strongly that Sy is part &#8220;twig&#8221; or part of some broader creation.  </p>
<p>The water is often referenced as being kept in wooden containers.  Water is also described as wearing away the mortar.  If Sylvester is of wood, then perhaps he contains water inside himself.  Something inside Sylvester could be the secret to destroying or controlling the stitched creations.  Water is part of helping life flourish.  Maybe Sy&#8217;s essence is needed for life across the planet to flourish again.  Life is currently shown to be dead.  The plants are all red.  That&#8217;s a pretty big signal that life is sick.  Interestingly, Sy thinks the venom should be green.  It&#8217;s making it sound like normal life and green is bad.  </p>
<p>Note also Sy&#8217;s reaction to the water running down his back &#8211; it doesn&#8217;t destroy him but it is called out:  &#8220;Rain poured down on me, tracing its way down the back of my neck, beneath my shirt.  The waxed and waterproof cowl and short cloak had kept my shirt dry, and I shivered at the sensation.&#8221;  Water proves to be part of the solution here &#8211; washing the pheromones off the snake charmer and being implied about how to deal with the stitched horses.</p>
<p>Another thing is that trees usually imply elevation.  The about page says &#8220;for those on the ground.&#8221;  That means on the forest floor.  Or not up in the ivory tower of the academy.</p>
</div>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>Ok thoughts:<br />
I&#8217;m betting the &#8220;children&#8221; are all academy students. They *might* have started out as kids, or they may not have. Important thing is they look like kids right now. I&#8217;m personally more betting on something to slow aging than something to change apparent age.<br />
Reasoning<br />
-fairly consistent, casual references to the books around, and ability to read suggest education i.e. not urchins<br />
-Sly was lying to that other kid, has no intention of letting him join their gang, likely lying about the nature of their gang<br />
-&#8220;the academy sends their regards&#8221;<br />
-if they were actually intending to report this guy they wouldn&#8217;t have killed him</p>
<p>Stitches &#8211; more likely to be modified slaves with broken brains than super-people, ending up in this state as a payment for debts or punishment for crime<br />
-apparently they can &#8220;start remembering stuff&#8221;, suggesting they do not typically have memories<br />
*stitched horses: actually horses? or people modded to be horse-like?</p>
<p>The academy is intentionally spreading the idea that you need to experiment to get in, harvesting the results and killing the creators. Admission criteria is actually based on something else.<br />
-I don&#8217;t actually have support for this, but the fact that they didn&#8217;t kill the snake by the end of the chapter could suggest as much. I&#8217;d expect they&#8217;d be more interested in the books though.<br />
-Though, it could explain why a bunch of students are out scientist-hunting &#8211; good way to get ahead of your peers (stealing work instead of working yourself)</p>
<p>*loving the structural vines, indication of more sophisticated gen-mod than stitching stuff together. The snake seemed pretty smooth, too.</p>
</div>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>Your comment and the about section makes me think that someone (The Academies?) have successfully started affecting large portions of the population in this generation of kids.  See this sentence: &#8220;It is only this generation, they say, that the youth and children are able to take the mad changes in stride, accepting it all as a part of day to day life.&#8221;  </p>
<p>Also, it&#8217;s pretty clear that the kids are either unconcerned about the authorities knowing that they let someone be killed or probably more likely that the Academy or someone wants experimenters dead.  What&#8217;s interesting is that the kids seem to have more blessing from the Academy while the Snake Charmer thought that experimenting would help him get in their good graces.  It feels a bit like a clean up crew &#8211; the kids have specifically ID&#8217;d problematic Stitches to help shut them down.  The snake monster eating a person might threaten the seemingly benevolent front of the academy so they have to eliminate people without control like the Snake Charmer.</p>
<p>Also interesting to note that the Snake Charmer is nicknamed similar to the Butcher and Mother Hen.  I was thinking those other two were stitches, but the nickname creates an association.</p>
<p>More broadly the only apparent authority/governing structure at work seems to be the Academy and its resources.  No one mentions the law or government or whatever.  </p>
<p>Another reading is that the kids are actively working to undermine the academy and it&#8217;s a HUGE coup that Lillian is associated with them.  Helping to kill agents of the Academy (such as the snake charmer, butcher, and mother hen) would match with them being an underground rebellious group.  That would also explain Jamie&#8217;s statement that Sy didn&#8217;t tell Thom the truth despite getting him involved.  The mission Sy created for Thom seems obviously designed to harm/inconvenience an agent or contact of the Academy.</p>
</div>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>More on the subject of Wildbow EATING KITTENS:<br />
We don&#8217;t actually know that they are kittens. They are referred to as kitties; not an unheard of word for cats, but unusual, and given the setting it might signify that they aren&#8217;t actual cats but are instead some kind of fabricated abomination. Thus, it might not be quite so horrible as I thought.<br />
However, the reaction of Lillian to the sight signifies that these things are at least viewed approximately the same as kittens in-universe.</p>
</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-233">
		<article id="comment-233" class="comment">
			<footer>
				<div class="comment-author vcard">
					<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e3b4307f47e58ba79791bd6f6c2d483c?s=50&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-50' height='50' width='50' />					<cite class="fn">notes</cite> |
					<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
						<a href="https://twigserial.wordpress.com/2014/12/24/taking-root-1-1/#comment-233"><time pubdate datetime="2015-03-10T18:58:14+00:00">
						March 10, 2015 at 6:58 pm						</time></a>
											</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->

				</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard -->
							</footer>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>Won&#8217;t be productive on work in the transition. Thus!</p>
<p>Strong opening ¶; good flow, good sense (I think! Hard to tell if it sets up expectations well without seeing what follows, but there&#8217;s a nice headfake at the classical four elements with &#8216;uninitiated&#8217; before committing to CHON, and that sets up a magi-science vibe.)</p>
<p>3rd ¶ is very clipped. Not sure what the aim is with that, but it recurs throughout the chapter. Repeated short declarative sentences. Style? Something about the POV? Can&#8217;t tell yet.</p>
<p>Wallace&#8217;s Law &#8211; not Darwin, not in this world.</p>
<p>Geography&#8217;s a bit odd: implication is that the group came in and then went the hayloft route, leaving their shoes with Jamie until their return. Why? What did they gain, beyond laying eyes on a large venomous serpent? And if so, why did they want to do that?</p>
<p>Sy/Sly variations intended? Sy to Gordon, Sly to Jamie? Or Sy as friend, Sly when he&#8217;s pulling a trick they&#8217;d rather he not?</p>
<p>Not representing the academy, or not as an independent contractor for money&#8230; and running a game of some kind, unknown to his teammates.</p>
<p>Stitched need protection from rain, apparently&#8230; why? Water&#8217;s a fantastic solvent, but unless biology has gotten a lot weirder, the stitched are still mostly water internally. Everyone wearing waterproof wax&#8230; but Sylvester not protecting his head.</p>
<p>Stitched = chimeras, apparently.</p>
<p>Hiding while close good way to build tension.</p>
<p>Italics use is interesting. Some for thoughts or whispers, or reading, others at emphases that are odd. Not bad, not wrong&#8230; odd. Frequent. E.g. <i>deliberate</i>, or <i>his</i>, <i>hero</i>, or <i>floor</i>. Effect is of someone else highlighting unexpected parts of the picture.</p>
<p>Use for emphases in speech shows vocal rhythms: effective; no criticism there beyond the stock issue of &#8216;does the dialogue sound aloud as intended&#8217;?</p>
<p>Lillian as a student of the Academy&#8230; the others as products of it? Or Lillian as both?</p>
<p>Very deliberate, cruel execution. Why? No one to see. Didn&#8217;t dispose of the &#8216;snake.&#8217; Didn&#8217;t take his research, either&#8230; left it there. What set of motives require them to remove the man, but leave his research and experiments? It&#8217;s not about the child eaten by the snake, or they wouldn&#8217;t have left the snake alive.</p>
<p>Will an official investigation find that the man died in a tragic lab accident, as so many non-Academics do, and then officially remove the &#8216;snake&#8217; and the research materials?<br />
Because otherwise, this is just&#8230; odd.</p>
<p>Flavor is interesting.</p>
</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-234">
		<article id="comment-234" class="comment">
			<footer>
				<div class="comment-author vcard">
					<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/3517eabb913d4e0740f74a8cc188d47b?s=50&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-50' height='50' width='50' />					<cite class="fn">Ardhanareeshwara</cite> |
					<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
						<a href="https://twigserial.wordpress.com/2014/12/24/taking-root-1-1/#comment-234"><time pubdate datetime="2015-03-10T19:14:01+00:00">
						March 10, 2015 at 7:14 pm						</time></a>
											</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->

				</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard -->
							</footer>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>Wildbow: I want to bring up a serious concern that I felt also with Pact, but much less with Worm (which I loved). Namely, you have a tendency of sometimes producing very wordy verbal descriptions of physical settings that are not very easy to read, and really distract from the telling of the story. Here is an example right at the beginning of Twig:</p>
<p>&#8220;What had once been a barn had been made into a warehouse, then abandoned partway through a third set of changes.  A floor of old wooden slats reached only halfway down the length of the old building, what had once been a hayloft.  If we stood on the edge, we could look down at the floor below to see uneven floorboards on top of compacted dirt.  The original barn’s door was still there, mounted on rollers.  I leaned over to get a better look.  I could see a table, some scattered papers, books, and a blackboard.  The only light was that which came in through windows.  A scattered set placed on the upper floor, and more well above head height on the lower one.&#8221;</p>
<p>Convoluted wording, hard to picture precisely. Very much an element of the writing in Pact that I had serious trouble with. And&#8211; I would suggest&#8211; absolutely not the sort of thing you want in one of the first paragraphs of a new story, where you are looking to ensnare readers without long descriptions of setting (unless such descriptions were really compelling, which this is not).</p>
<p>Perhaps the hardest thing for me as a reader when I come across these descriptions is why you considered those particular physical details so important as to put on paper. I would like for physical descriptions to be much more natural and organic, and flow seamlessly with the story itself.</p>
<p>Anyway, that&#8217;s my honest feedback as a longtime reader.</p>
<p>Wishing you all the best with your new venture, and I will continue to read what you write and support your efforts as long as possible.</p>
</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-237">
		<article id="comment-237" class="comment">
			<footer>
				<div class="comment-author vcard">
					<img alt='' src='https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/3517eabb913d4e0740f74a8cc188d47b?s=50&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-50' height='50' width='50' />					<cite class="fn">Ardhanareeshwara</cite> |
					<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
						<a href="https://twigserial.wordpress.com/2014/12/24/taking-root-1-1/#comment-237"><time pubdate datetime="2015-03-10T20:29:32+00:00">
						March 10, 2015 at 8:29 pm						</time></a>
											</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->

				</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard -->
							</footer>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>While I am about it, let me mention a few more (hopefully constructive) criticisms:</p>
<p>1) Use of italics: This seems rather forced, and not something that I like stylistically except in very exceptional circumstances. Both in Pact and in the first chapter of Twig, italics have been used a bit too much. They confer too much emphasis on things that are after all not that important.</p>
<p>2) More on why the wordy descriptions bother me: They confer an omniscience on the narrator that sits uncomfortably with me. Why should the narrator know all those physical details, such as about the history of a place? One could argue that some of these things are deducible, but many of the descriptions sound a bit too specific or definitive.</p>
<p>Hope that helps.</p>
</div>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>From the updated post on Worm&#8217;s site, there is confirmation that this is an update of the Boil setting: </p>

<p>I’ve now moved on to the writing of Twig, with the first chapter released just fourteen hours ago.  Those who read the sample story Boil between the writing of Worm and Pact may see familiar elements – critiques of Boil often said they liked the world but weren’t grabbed by the character, who was perhaps a little similar to Taylor.  In Twig, I’ve aimed to keep what worked and rework what didn’t, and early reception seems positive.</p>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>I really liked this first chapter. It feels much more like this world is already esrltablished and the readers are jumping into it, rather than it being constricted as the story is written. Was anyone else struck by the importance of water? I expect that it reacts badly with &#8220;stitched&#8221; things and that&#8217;s why the kids covered themselves in wax. Snake charmer just didn&#8217;t know they were fake kids so he thought it was to hide the smell. There is a lot of attention put on the rain, rain barrels, and gutters. There was also that line about dumping water on stitched horses to cause problems. Why would horses need raincoats unless water is an issue?</p>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>I actually just finished my second reading of Worm(including all the comments!) a couple of days ago when I went back to Pact, which I intended to try to catch up so I could read the end with the other commenters, only to see, to my dismay, that Epilogue had already been posted! I&#8217;m still going to read Pact, of course, but at the same time as Twig. </p>
<p>Worm, by the way, was amazing and consumed half my life reading through it. Not much else to say that hasn&#8217;t been said in far better ways by others, but I&#8217;ll definitely be looking forward to the ebook/dead tree versions! And the sequel. And the inevitable next rereading&#8230; (not necessarily in that order)</p>
<p>I&#8217;m incredibly excited about reading Twig right from the beginning, along with the rest of the you in the comments! I bet it&#8217;s going to be an awesome ride. Thoughts:<br />
&#8211; The beginning is significantly different from Worm and Pact, in that the protagonist starts off with a well-established team, instead of being more or less alone. Really interested in seeing how this changes things&#8230; Also, I think I prefer this opening over Pact&#8217;s, maybe because it was more engaging. Also, I can tell there&#8217;s going to be lots of worldbuilding, which was one of my favourite parts of Worm<br />
&#8211; I agree that Helen, at least, is/was stitched (avoidance of water, &#8220;special case&#8221;)<br />
&#8211; What exactly does the Academy do, and what&#8217;s its relation to this group? Maybe they created Helen, considering her last lines about the Academy sending its regards. Or maybe the Academy created/had a hand in the creation of all of the main 5(I think the Academy is paying them, at the very least). Which leads me to&#8230;<br />
-Lilian &#8211; she&#8217;s constantly referred to as new, and not one of them, whose job is to keep them in one piece&#8230;. maybe she&#8217;s the only one that wasn&#8217;t stitched? She&#8217;s the only one that&#8217;s bothered about Snake Charmer&#8217;s death, while she was fixing up Sy(who is most likely at least partly stitched, he wasn&#8217;t bothered about the venom like normal people would), and, maybe a little meta, but there are only 5 figures in the top banner, so it makes me wonder what&#8217;s going to happen to her, or someone else&#8230;<br />
-Character death in the first chapter! Yay!<br />
-Rereading it, water definitely seems like it plays an important role, but what&#8217;s up with the new growths that are red, and everything else is dead or something? Perhaps contamination/pollution, from the factory?<br />
-The art is looking really cool! Looking forward to the banner on TWB and voting for Twig there(Wildbow&#8217;s most likely going to dominate the top 10 within a decade or so). </p>
<p>I&#8217;d really love to donate, but don&#8217;t have the funds to at the moment, so I&#8217;ll help out in other ways for now, such as typoing!<br />
&#8211; &#8220;without a without prominent ridge&#8221; Extra &#8216;without&#8217; there.</p>
<p>Just wondering, is there a difference between the Worm and Pact spoilers in the cipher? I don&#8217;t want to get spoiled for Pact, but I&#8217;ve read Worm, so I was wondering what/if there&#8217;s a difference.<br />
So excited for Saturday!<br />
Wildbow is awesome, you magnificent bastard. That is all.</p>
</div>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>I like the story and the setting.<br />
The very beginning seems off just a little. The thoughts that Sylvester begins with seem odd when you  consider the nature of the situation he is in: &#8220;How does it go?  The first lesson, something even the uninitiated know.  For life to flourish on the most basic level, it requires four elements.  Carbon, oxygen, nitrogen and hydrogen.  We were doing fine on that count.  The air around us was stale, but it was still oxygen.  Water ran around and below us, flowing over our bare feet, redirected from gutters to the building’s inside.&#8221;</p>
<p>My first thought was that Sylvester and his group were colonists on a new planet. But that didn&#8217;t quite jive with the thoughts he was having about the barn and the creature in it. Then, they almost seemed like people who had just been awakened, with knowledge of certain things, but being uncertain of other things. It wasn&#8217;t until they started going down the side of the building and then met Jamie and Thomas that it became clear that they were on a mission. </p>
<p>I&#8217;m not entirely sure how much of that was intentional, or just me being obtuse. It didn&#8217;t make me not like the story, but it did confuse me for a little bit.</p>
</div>

	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 highlander-comment" id="li-comment-329">
		<article id="comment-329" class="comment">
			<footer>
				<div class="comment-author vcard">
					<img alt='' src='https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b7d616828bfb391d7fb0ab6cf2e4ed2a?s=50&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-50' height='50' width='50' />					<cite class="fn">Nidhogg</cite> |
					<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
						<a href="https://twigserial.wordpress.com/2014/12/24/taking-root-1-1/#comment-329"><time pubdate datetime="2015-03-13T00:59:55+00:00">
						March 13, 2015 at 12:59 am						</time></a>
											</span><!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->

				</div><!-- .comment-author .vcard -->
							</footer>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>New story, and a promising one, too.</p>
<p>From what I can see here, I already like the protagonist better then I liked Worm&#8217;s or Pact&#8217;s. Don&#8217;t get me wrong, Taylor and Blake were each compelling in their own way, but I&#8217;m something of a sucker for trickery and plots, and that&#8217;s not really an element that either of them could bring to the table. Taylor is intelligent, and a master of leveraging force against her foes, but she was rather lacking in the &#8220;methods of success besides force&#8221; department. Blake and Rose were both a bit better with that, but the situation they were in was set up so that they were so busy with other people&#8217;s plans that they could never really make their own. From what I can see here, Sy is very much a trickster, and I like that. </p>
<p>Water is clearly bad for stitched, and there&#8217;s some evidence here that the children (besides Lilian) are, themselves, stitched. From Sy&#8217;s behavior, he seems determined to ignore the danger. I see three possible reasons for this (note that these are not mutually exclusive):<br />
1) aversion to water is psychological, and Sy is working to over come it<br />
2)  A tolerance of sorts to water&#8217;s detrimental effects if one is dedicated enough to suffer from it in the mean time (This also begs the question of why water is damaging. My best guess is that a catalyst for chemical reactions like water is not something you want near delicate artifical biochemistry)<br />
3) Sy is dangerously reckless of his own health and well being</p>
<p>I&#8217;m guessing that stitched is a term for someone who&#8217;s been Bonesaw&#8217;d in one sense or another. Given the comment about the &#8220;stitched who regained his memories&#8221; the process apparently causes amnesia, which is probably going to be pretty relevant. </p>
<p>The repeated comments about how Gordon was &#8220;the hero&#8221; the talented one, suggests bitterness, irony (Gordon and/or Sy are not what they seem, even by stitched standards) or both.</p>
<p>Golden gets used as an adjetive an awful lot. An element of the setting, perhaps?</p>
</div>

				<div class="comment-author vcard">
					<img alt='' src='https://1.gravatar.com/avatar/4039b7313107468d45cd61ed65759ca2?s=50&#038;d=identicon&#038;r=G' class='avatar avatar-50' height='50' width='50' />					<cite class="fn"><a href='http://archiveseven.wordpress.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>MinuSeveN</a></cite> |
					<span class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
						<a href="https://twigserial.wordpress.com/2014/12/24/taking-root-1-1/#comment-737"><time pubdate datetime="2015-03-20T09:06:19+00:00">

			<div class="comment-content"><p>Great start. The overall impression of the chapter itself is solid. There&#8217;s all the elements needed here for a gripping start and more than enough action and interaction for me to want to come back. I&#8217;m definitely liking it more than your other serials, but then again, this is only the first chapter. Is that a good thing?</p>
<p>Twig itself&#8230; I don&#8217;t know. There&#8217;s definitely mad science in the background. And the foreground. A feeling of old and new melding together to form a present that maybe shouldn&#8217;t be. I personally like the science being showcased, so that&#8217;s another point in my book. The kids are so very intelligent, yet they act like kids at times. But only at times. Sly is like his name, Gordon gives out a solid impression, Lillian comes out as scared and cute, Jamie(es?)&#8217;s the sensible/quiet one and Helen the creepy, always there for you teammate. I do wonder if Thomas will reappear. It&#8217;s obvious the central cast ARE the Academy&#8217;s people, so will this kid make more contact with them? Become an informant, something closer? On the whole, this read somewhat like CSI or a &#8220;get the culprit&#8221; story. Politics of some sort are quite clearly visible in the future. And, at the expense of dragging the past into this, it&#8217;s soooooo nice to be on the side of the Law this time. I hope.</p>
<p>The main mystery (for me) is what are they? Not biologically or anything, I&#8217;d like to think they&#8217;re &#8220;regular&#8221; humans for a change, but what kind of people are all these &#8220;scientists&#8221;, these alchemists and builders and probable madmen and women? There is the Academy. How does that work too?</p>
<p>&#8230; and I should maybe start reading the next chapter instead of blindly speculating.</p>
<p>Also. What will become of the hybrid now that its creator is dead?</p>
</div>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>&#8230;but Deedee blows his experiments, to smithereens! There is doom and gloom while things go boom!&#8230;.in Dexter&#8217;s Lab!</p>
<p>Welcome to Twig. For those playing along at home, this is when you load up Geneforge.</p>
<p>Nice to know I didn&#8217;t miss anything by showing up late. Looks like the story was already in media res.</p>
<p>So this is Twig, apparently, where we join a pack of sociopathic prepubescents wandering around playing doctor with each other while trying to avoid becoming a victim of an older man&#8217;s pet snake. He&#8217;d have gotten away with it, too, if it wasn&#8217;t for those meddling kids and their insatiable love of Barbie cosplay. At least we know for a fact that somebody waxed those asses. Wax on, wax off. Except for when the older guy grabbed for Gordon, in which case it was jacket on, jacket off. Not that our POV character could tell us that much about it after the older man splashed fluids all over the kid. Then, of course, one of the girls washed him off in the shower. </p>
<p>And for those looking for an indication of the tone of the story: yes, that&#8217;s a monster eating kittens right from the very beginning. </p>
<p>Now, let&#8217;s go see how these kids like getting to that special time in their bodies&#8217; development when they learn to release their own personal krakens.</p>
</div>

			<div class="comment-content"><p>I Finally start the last of Wilbow&#8217;s mea&#8230;err,stories.I kinda do not want to catch up,means I&#8217;d have to wait.That said,it seems curious,up till now,</p>
<p>Wilbow&#8217;s series seem inversely interesting, relative to his other stories at least, to how much I like the setting.I love magic,dislike superheroes and biopunk,yet ttill now,I liked Pact less&#8230;.though I think it has the most interesting setting,so I hope very much Wilbow revisits it when he is more mature as a writer.That said &#8220;liked it less&#8221;is like saying &#8220;Saturn is smaller than Jupiter&#8221;,it by no means mean it was in any way bad.</p>
<p>Biology,huh&#8230;.I kinda dislike theme that are realistic but in the future,I prefer heroes to have either potentially unlimited power to gain,or absolute superpowers with strange effects &#8230;That said,I have learned never to judge by gendre and also,to always trust Wilbow&#8230;.he can make a food you are allergic too and you won&#8217;t be able to stop eating&#8230;.crap,again I slipped a food analogy there.</p>
<p>Sylvester is the MC huh&#8230;I hope he gets to fight a bioeingeenered yellow bird,perhaps one with compartments to pull out weapons like hammers,or better yet an augumented canary&#8230;.and upon beating it,eating it.</p>

<script type="text/javascript">
var highlander_expando_javascript = function(){
	var input = document.createElement( 'input' ),
	    comment = jQuery( '#comment' );

	if ( 'placeholder' in input ) {
		comment.attr( 'placeholder', jQuery( '.comment-textarea label' ).remove().text() );
	}

	// Expando Mode: start small, then auto-resize on first click + text length
	jQuery( '#comment-form-identity' ).hide();
	jQuery( '#comment-form-subscribe' ).hide();
	jQuery( '#commentform .form-submit' ).hide();

	comment.css( { 'height':'10px' } ).one( 'focus', function() {
		var timer = setInterval( HighlanderComments.resizeCallback, 10 )
		jQuery( this ).animate( { 'height': HighlanderComments.initialHeight } ).delay( 100 ).queue( function(n) { clearInterval( timer ); HighlanderComments.resizeCallback(); n(); } );
		jQuery( '#comment-form-identity' ).slideDown();
		jQuery( '#comment-form-subscribe' ).slideDown();
		jQuery( '#commentform .form-submit' ).slideDown();
	});
}
jQuery(document).ready( highlander_expando_javascript );
</script>
